INTRODUCTION


Ron Müller & Associates (RMA) has conducted this Traffic Impact and Access Study to
evaluate the effects from, and identify improvements for, the redevelopment of several adjoining
parcels of land located at 202 & 204 Arsenal Street, 56 & 58 Irving Street, and 70 Phillips Street
in Watertown, Massachusetts. As currently envisioned, the existing vacant industrial building
with an address at 56 & 58 Irving Street, and a small retail/commercial building located at 202-
204 Arsenal Street, which aggregate approximately 150,000 square feet, will be razed and
several new buildings will be constructed including a 40,000 square foot supermarket and 307
apartment units. One of the apartment buildings will also contain approximately 6,000 square
feet of retail space on the first floor abutting Arsenal Street and was therefore included in this
study.

Access to the site has historically been provided from an existing driveway on Birch Road, a
residential street, and more recently an additional driveway on Arsenal Street near the eastern
portion of the property, offset from the Beechwood Avenue intersection. A third access point is
available via a 30-foot wide driveway easement which crosses adjacent property located at 56
Irving Street (M.J. Pirolli & Sons, Inc. Masonry Supply) and provides access to Irving Street to
the west. With redevelopment of the site, the existing Arsenal Street driveway will be used as
the main driveway for the apartment buildings on the easterly site parcel, the gated driveway
onto Birch Road will be eliminated, and a new signalized full access driveway will be
constructed on Arsenal Street approximately midway between the Irving Street and Beechwood
Avenue intersections to service the supermarket.

As part of a development agreement with the abutter to the west, Webster Yard Realty Trust
("Webster" property), a portion of their existing development would share its access with the


13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                        Page 1
Ron Müller & Associates                                                 Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                 Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




redevelopment project. The Webster property currently contains three separate buildings which
share access via Parker Street and Phillips Street, both residential streets. These buildings
include a ±2,000 square foot two-story office building, an ±18,400 square foot self-storage
facility, and a ±29,000 square foot mixed use building. Under proposed conditions, the office
building and the portion of the self-storage facility to remain (±13,000 square feet) will continue
to share access via Parker Street and Phillips Street. However, the ±29,000 square foot mixed
use former industrial building will share parking and access to Arsenal Street with the proposed
redevelopment project. The proposed site design will include a vehicular barrier preventing
direct access from Arsenal Street to either Phillips or Parker Streets, therefore under proposed
conditions, vehicles will not be able to access the proposed parking provided for the new
supermarket and the existing ±29,000 square foot mixed used building on the Webster property
via Parker or Phillips Streets. This will result in a significant reduction in existing vehicle traffic
through the residential neighborhoods. For purposes of this study, the existing ±29,000 square
foot building are evaluated as a 28,000 square foot retail building in order to provide for a
conservative analysis and allow for the possible expansion and re-use of this building in the
future.

In addition, the proponent also has a development agreement with M.J. Pirolli & Sons, Inc.
Masonry Supply that allows access to the site from Arsenal Street via an easement over Pirolli
land. That easement and site access will then also allow for the potential redevelopment of the
Pirolli property. It is currently envisioned that up to 15,000 square feet of retail space and 302
apartment units could be constructed on the Pirolli land. Although access may also be provided
from the Pirolli site onto Irving Street to service a portion of the retail and apartments proposed
on that site, for the purpose of this study and to present a conservative analytical scenario, all site
traffic from the Pirolli property was assume to enter and exit via the main westerly driveway.

This study therefore evaluates the effects on the roadway network of a total of 83,000 square feet
of retail space and 302 apartment units to be constructed and using the proposed new access
drive on Arsenal Street (midway between Irving Street and Beechwood Avenue); and 307
apartment units and 6,000 square feet of retail space to be constructed and using the existing
(easterly) driveway on Arsenal Street opposite Beechwood Avenue. The site location in relation
to the surrounding roadways is shown on Figure 1.

This study provides an estimate of the expected trip generation and distribution characteristics of
the project, evaluates the impact of those trips on Arsenal Street and nearby intersections, and
determines the necessity for improvements to the area roadway system. As documented in this
report, ample capacity exists at the study area intersections to accommodate the proposed
development with the implementation of several improvements that are recommended to
enhance roadway and intersection capacity and safety of all road users. These include:

EXISTING CONDITIONS


Study Area

Evaluation of the effects on the roadway network from redevelopment of the site as proposed
requires an evaluation of existing and projected volumes, the additional vehicular demand
generated by the project, and the effect that those vehicle trips will have on the adjacent streets.
In preparing this study for the site, the following intersections were analyzed and evaluated:

      ·     Arsenal Street at School Street
      ·     Arsenal Street at Beechwood Avenue
      ·     Arsenal Street at Irving Street
      ·     North Beacon Street at Beechwood Avenue
      ·     Mount Auburn Street at Irving Street and Palfrey Street

The proposed development is expected to have a minimal effect on the roadways beyond this
study area, with volume increases ranging from less than one to four additional vehicles per
minute on the major roadways during peak hours.




13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                                Page 4
Ron Müller & Associates                                               Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services               Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




Traffic Volumes

Base conditions within the study area were developed by conducting automatic traffic recorder
(ATR) counts on Arsenal Street, as well as manual turning movement and vehicle classification
counts (TMCs) at the study area intersections. All counts were conducted in June 2013 while
schools were still in session and are provided in the Appendix. The ATR counts were performed
for a 72-hour period to collect weekday and Saturday daily volumes and the TMCs were
performed during the weekday AM peak period (7:00 to 9:00 AM), the weekday PM peak period
(4:00 to 6:00 PM), and the Saturday midday peak period (11:00 AM to 2:00 PM) to collect peak
hour data.

The count data indicate that the weekday AM peak hour generally occurs from 8:00 to 9:00 AM,
the weekday PM peak hour generally occurs from 5:00 to 6:00 PM and the Saturday midday
peak hour generally occurs from 11:45 AM to 12:45 PM. However, to present a conservative
analytical framework, the individual intersection peak hours were used in this report to present
the highest peak hour volumes at each location.

To determine if the count data needed to be adjusted to represent annual average month
conditions consistent with state guidelines for traffic impact assessment, historical traffic volume
data were obtained from the Massachusetts Department of Transportation (MassDOT). Based on
the closest permanent traffic count station to the project site (Station 4118 located on I-95 in
Lexington), traffic during the month of June is approximately 3.5 percent above annual average
month traffic conditions. Therefore, the June collected data were used without adjustment to
represent above annual average conditions. The MassDOT seasonal adjustment data are
provided in the Appendix and the weekday and Saturday daily and peak hour volumes are
summarized in Table 1. The 2013 Existing peak hour flow networks are provided on Figures 2,
3, and 4, representing weekday AM, weekday PM, and Saturday midday peak hour conditions,
respectively.

Accidents

Accident data for the study area intersections were obtained from MassDOT for the period
between 2009 and 2011, the latest three years of available data. A summary of the MassDOT
accident data at the study area intersections is provided in Table 2. In addition to the summary,
accident occurrence should also be compared to the volume of traffic through a particular
intersection to determine any significance. Accordingly, the accident rate was calculated for
each intersection and compared with the statewide and district-wide averages. An intersection
accident rate is a measure of the frequency of accidents compared to the vehicular volume
through an intersection and is presented in accidents per million entering vehicles (acc/mev).
For signalized intersections, the statewide average accident rate is 0.80 acc/mev and the district-
wide accident rate is 0.76 acc/mev. For unsignalized intersections, the statewide average
accident rate is 0.60 acc/mev and the district-wide accident rate is 0.58 acc/mev. A comparison
of the calculated accident rate to the statewide and district-wide averages can be used to establish
the significance of accident occurrence and whether or not potential safety problems exist. The
crash rate worksheets are provided in the Appendix.

   As shown in Table 2, the highest number of crashes occurred at the Arsenal Street and Irving

   the elapsed time into the measured distance between checkpoints. The results of the speed
   measurements are summarized in Table 3.

As shown in Table 3, average speeds on Arsenal Street are slightly higher than the posted speed
limit, but 85th percentile speeds are six to seven miles per hour higher than the posted limit.
Since the majority of vehicles are traveling faster than the posted speed limit, the sight distance
requirements should be based on these higher speeds to assure safe operation of the new
driveway, as discussed below.


Sight Distance

To identify potential safety concerns associated with site access and egress, sight distances have
been evaluated at the existing and proposed site driveway locations to determine if the available
sight distances for vehicles exiting the site meet or exceed the minimum distances required for
approaching vehicles to safely stop. The available sight distances were compared with minimum
requirements, as established by the American Association of State Highway and Transportation
Officials (AASHTO)1. AASHTO is the national standard by which vehicle sight distance is
calculated, measured, and reported. The MassDOT and the Executive Office of Energy and
Environmental Affairs (EEA) require the use of AASHTO sight distance standards as stated in
their guidelines.

Sight distance is the length of roadway ahead that is visible to the driver. Stopping Sight
Distance (SSD) is the minimum distance required for a vehicle traveling at a certain speed to
safely stop before reaching a stationary object in its path. The values are based on a driver
perception and reaction time of 2.5 seconds and a braking distance calculated for wet, level
pavements. When the roadway is either on an upgrade or downgrade, grade correction factors are
applied. Stopping sight distance is measured from an eye height of 3.5 feet to an object height of
2 feet above street level, equivalent to the taillight height of a passenger car. The SSD is
measured along the centerline of the traveled way of the major road.

1
    A Policy on Geometric Design of Highways and Streets; American Association of State Highway and
    Transportation Officials (AASHTO); 2004.


13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                                                      Page 8
Ron Müller & Associates                                                Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




Intersection sight distance (ISD) is provided on minor street approaches to allow the drivers of
stopped vehicles a sufficient view of the major roadway to decide when to enter the major
roadway. By definition, ISD is the minimum distance required for a motorist exiting a minor
street to turn onto the major street, without being overtaken by an approaching vehicle reducing
its speed from the design speed to 70 percent of the design speed. ISD is measured from an eye
height of 3.5 feet to an object height of 3.5 feet above street level. The use of an object height
equal to the driver eye height makes intersection sight distances reciprocal (i.e., if one driver can
see another vehicle, then the driver of that vehicle can also see the first vehicle). When the minor
street is on an upgrade that exceeds 3 percent, grade correction factors are applied.

SSD is generally more important as it represents the minimum distance required for safe
stopping while ISD is based only upon acceptable speed reductions to the approaching vehicles.
However, the ISD must be equal to or greater than the minimum required SSD in order to
provide safe operations at the intersection. In accordance with the AASHTO manual, "If the
available sight distance for an entering or crossing vehicle is at least equal to the appropriate
stopping sight distance for the major road, then drivers have sufficient sight distance to
anticipate and avoid collisions. However, in some cases, this may require a major-road vehicle
to stop or slow to accommodate the maneuver by a minor-road vehicle. To enhance traffic
operations, intersection sight distances that exceed stopping sight distances are desirable along
the major road." Accordingly, ISD should be at least equal to the distance required to allow a
driver approaching the minor road to safely stop.

The available SSD and ISD at the existing and proposed site driveway locations were measured
and compared to minimum requirements as established by AASHTO. Since the requirements are
based on the speed of vehicles on the adjacent streets, the results of the vehicle speed study on
Arsenal Street were used for this purpose. The required minimum sight distances for these
speeds are compared to the available distances, as shown in Table 4.

As shown in the table, ample sight distance exists to the east and west of both the existing east
site driveway, which is proposed to be included into the existing Beechwood Avenue signal
operation, and the proposed west site driveway. Therefore, safe operation of both driveway
locations can be expected. Any proposed landscaping or signs in the vicinity of the driveways
should be kept low to the ground (less than 3 feet above street level) or set back sufficiently so as
not to impede sight distances for drivers exiting the site.

FUTURE CONDITIONS


Traffic Growth

Future traffic conditions were projected to the year 2018, representing a 5-year design horizon
consistent with local and state requirements for traffic impact analysis. To project traffic
conditions within this design horizon, two components of traffic growth were included. First, an
annual average traffic growth rate was determined to account for general population growth and
smaller development projects (i.e. residential subdivisions) that may impact traffic in the site
vicinity. Based on permanent traffic count station data collected by MassDOT on I-95 in
Lexington (Station 4118) between 2006 and 2009, traffic volumes have been declining at an
average rate of 1.4 percent per year. However, this trend may not continue into the future. To
provide a conservative (worse-case) analysis scenario, a 1.0 percent annual growth rate was used
consistent with other recent studies performed in Watertown.

Second, any planned or approved specific developments in the area that would generate a
significant volume of traffic on study area roadways within the next five years were included.
Based on discussions with local officials, there were nine projects identified in the area.
However, seven of the nine projects are located in or near Waltham and are expected to have a
minimal impact on traffic within the study area. These projects were therefore assumed to be
accounted for within the background traffic growth rate and include:

Ron Müller & Associates                                               Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services               Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




Waltham
  · Residential Development ­ 200 apartments at the Seyon Sreet, Farewell Street, and River
      Street intersection
  · Residential Development ­ 16 townhouses at the corner of Grove Street and Seyon Street

Watertown
  · Alta at the Estate ­ 7 townhouses and 148 apartments under construction on Waltham
       Street at the Waltham Town Line
  · Riverbend ­ 170 apartments under construction on Pleasant Street
  · Repton Place (Phase II) ­ 206 apartments at 555 Pleasant Street
  · Riverworks ­ occupancy of the vacant office space (50% of the 203,400 sf) at the corner
       of Bridge Street and Pleasant Street
  · Assisted Living ­ 90 unit assisted living facility at the corner of Spring and Summer
       Street

The two projects identified in the area that are expected to result in an impact of traffic through
the study area in addition to the background traffic growth include:

Watertown
  · Condominiums ­ 30-unit condos at the corner of Mt. Auburn and Taylor Streets
  · Residential/Retail ­ 70-unit apartment building and 10,000 square feet of retail space
       between Howard and Beacon Streets

It was assumed that all of these developments are to be completed and occupied within the 5-
year design horizon. The trip generation and distribution assumptions for these two projects are
provided in the Appendix.


No-Build Conditions

The 2018 No-Build networks were accordingly developed by applying a compounded 1.0
percent annual growth rate (5.1 percent over five years) to the existing adjacent street volumes as
well as the traffic expected to be generated by the two additional development projects. The
2018 No-Build peak-hour flow networks are shown in Figures 5, 6, and 7 for the weekday AM,
weekday PM, and Saturday midday peak hours, respectively.


Trip Generation

The proposed development consists of razing the existing industrial, mixed use space and
commercial/retail buildings on the site. Although the site does generate some amount of traffic
and the existing uses could be re-occupied by right, no credit was taken for these trips to provide
a conservative (worst-case sceanrio) analysis condition. The existing uses do have access onto
area local streets which will either be closed or restricted to emergency access only as part of the



13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                         Page 11
Ron Müller & Associates                                                          Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                          Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




proposed project redevelopment.                This will provide an additional benefit to the area
neighborhoods.

To estimate the volume of traffic to be generated by the proposed development, data contained in
the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) Trip Generation Manual2 were used. The
westerly portion of the site will include a 40,000 square foot supermarket, 43,000 square feet of
additional retail space, and 302 apartment units with access and egress through a proposed
driveway to be located on Arsenal Street approximately midway between Irving Street and
Beechwood Avenue. Traffic generation for this portion of the site was estimated using ITE LUC
850 (Supermarket), ITE LUC 820 (Shopping Center), and ITE LUC 220 (Apartments).

The easterly portion of the site will include approximately 6,000 square feet of retail space and
307 apartment units with access to and egress from these uses to be provided through an existing
driveway on Arsenal Street slightly offset from Beechwood Avenue. Traffic generation for this
portion of the site was estimated using ITE LUC 826 (Specialty Retail) and ITE LUC 220
(Apartments). Although all the trips generated by the uses on the easterly parcel are expected to
enter and exit the driveway, there will be internal capture (or multi-use) trips on the westerly
parcel. Based on multi-use trip calculations described in the ITE Trip Generation Manual, there
is expected to be a 21% internal capture rate during the weekday AM peak hour, 32% internal
capture rate during the weekday PM peak hour, and a 33% internal capture rate for the Saturday
peak hours. An average of 26% was used for the weekday daily and 33% for the Saturday daily
internal capture rate estimates. All trip generation data and calculations are provided in the
Appendix.

Not all of the vehicle trips generated by the retail portions of the development represent new trips
on the study area roadway system. Studies have shown that retail developments generate a
substantial amount of their business from the traffic already present on the adjacent roadway.
These trips are referred to as pass-by trips. Based on data presented in the ITE Trip Generation
Manual, the average pass-by trip percentage for these uses can be up to 34 percent. However, to
be consistent with state guidelines, a pass-by rate of only 25 percent was used for the retail uses.
Table 5 summarizes the expected trip-generation characteristics of the westerly portion of the
project and Table 6 summarizes the trip-generation characteristics for the easterly parcel.

As shown in Table 5, the westerly site of the proposed project with access through the new
driveway is expected to generate 259 new vehicle trips (111 entering and 148 exiting) during the
weekday AM peak hour, 499 new vehicle trips (274 entering and 225 exiting) during the
weekday PM peak hour, and 611 new vehicle trips (322 entering and 289 exiting) during the
Saturday midday peak hour.

Trip Distribution

The distribution of new site trips was estimated based on a review of surrounding population
densities, available access routes to the site, and existing travel patterns based on the type of use.
Accordingly, two separate distribution patterns were developed, one for the retail portion of the
development and the other for the residential uses. For the retail uses, 25 percent of the retail site
traffic is expected to and from the east on Arsenal Street and 20 percent to and from the west.
Along North Beacon Street, 15 percent of the retail site traffic is expected to and from the east
and 15 percent of the retail site traffic is expected to and from the north on School Street. Of the
remaining 25 percent of the retail site traffic, 5 percent is expected to and from the south along
Irving Street and 20 percent to and from the north/east along Mt. Auburn Street and Palfrey
Street (one-way). The directional distribution of pass-by trips is expected to follow the existing
travel patterns on Arsenal Street. It should be noted that although on-street parking is proposed
for the 6,000 square feet of retail space that will be located adjacent to Arsenal Street on the
easterly project parcel, all site traffic was assumed to enter and exit the driveway to present a
conservative analytical scenario.

CAPACITY ANALYSIS


Level-of-service (LOS) analyses were conducted at the study area intersections under existing
and projected volume conditions to determine the effect that the site generated traffic will have
on intersection operations. The capacity analysis methodology is based on the concepts and
procedures in the Highway Capacity Manual3 (HCM) and is described in the Appendix. The
maximum back of queue during an average signal cycle and a 95th percentile signal cycle were
calculated for each lane group during the peak periods studied. The back of queue is the length
of a backup of vehicles from the stop line of a signalized intersection to the last car in the queue
that is required to stop, regardless of the signal indication. The length of this queue depends on a
number of factors including signal timing, vehicle arrival patterns, and the saturation flow rate.
For unsignalized intersections, the 95th percentile queue represents the length of queue of the
critical minor-street movement that is not expected to be exceeded 95 percent of the time during
the analysis period (typically one hour). In this case, the queue length is a function of the
capacity of the movement and the movement's degree of saturation.

The Synchro version 8.0 analysis program was used for all capacity analyses. However, the
2010 HCM method could not be used due to the permitted/protected left-turn phasing of several
of the traffic signals within the study area, which the 2010 HCM method does not support. The
level-of-service and queue results are presented in Table 9 and are discussed below. All analysis
worksheets are provided in the Appendix.

As shown in Table 9, all study intersections operate at acceptable levels during peak hours under
existing and design-year volume conditions, although the proposed development will degrade the
level of service and cause significant delays and queues at the Arsenal Street and Beechwood
Avenue intersection during the Saturday peak hour. Under STOP-sign control, both the east and
west site driveways would operate at unacceptable levels (LOS F) during the weekday PM and
Saturday midday peak hours. Improvements are therefore recommended at the site driveway
intersections.

           MITIGATION


           The final phase of the transportation analysis process is to identify improvement measures
           necessary to mitigate the effects of the project on the transportation system. Mitigation measures
           considered necessary to address existing and future roadway system deficiencies are discussed
           below as they relate to impacts as a result of background growth and the project. The project
           proponent has agreed to fund the design and construction of these measures.


           Arsenal Street at West Site Drive

           As documented in the previous section, turns exiting the proposed west site driveway would
           operate at LOS F under STOP-sign control. Accordingly, a traffic signal warrant analysis was
           conducted to determine if signal control could be installed at this location given the vehicular
           volumes expected to be generated by the proposed development. The hourly distribution of
           vehicles on Arsenal Street was based on the automatic traffic recorder counts. As documented
           previously, these volumes approximate annual average-month conditions and can therefore be
           used in this analysis without any adjustments, consistent with Manual on Uniform Traffic



           13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                                                Page 21
Ron Müller & Associates                                                         Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                        Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




Control Devices (MUTCD)4 guidelines. The hourly distribution of traffic to and from the retail
portion of the development was estimated using data provided in the ITE Trip Generation
Manual. The hourly distribution of the residential traffic was based on daily traffic counts
conducted at an existing residential development in Weymouth.5 The available traffic data were
compared with the requirements established in the MUTCD for the following volume-related
warrants:

       ·    Warrant 1 ­ Eight Hour Vehicular Volume
            o Condition A ­ Minimum Vehicular Volume
            o Condition B ­ Interruption of Continuous Traffic
            o Combination of Conditions A and B
       ·    Warrant 2 ­ Four-Hour Vehicular Volume; and
       ·    Warrant 3 ­ One-Hour Vehicular Volume.

The warrant analyses were performed without any reduction to the minimum volume
requirements as allowed in the MUTCD under certain conditions. The warrant analysis
worksheet is provided in the Appendix along with the hourly distribution of traffic from the retail
and residential portions of the westerly development area.

In accordance with the MUTCD, a traffic control signal may only be installed if at least one of
the signal warrants is met. However, a number of factors are involved in determining if signal
control should be installed, including intersection operations, safety, and engineering judgment.
It is only in very rare circumstances that a traffic control signal is installed on the basis of the
peak hour warrant alone. Normally, at least one of the eight-hour warrants (Warrant 1,
Condition A or B) should be met before signal control is considered. The peak-hour volume
warrant is applied only in unusual cases such as driveways serving large office/industrial
complexes, manufacturing plants, or high-occupancy vehicle facilities that attract or discharge
large numbers of vehicles over a short period of time. In addition, the combination of Conditions
A and B under Warrant 1 should only be applied after an adequate analysis of other alternatives.
Table 10 summarizes the results of the signal warrant analysis.


      Table 10
      Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis Summary


                                                    Warrant 1           Warrant    Warrant       Signal
                         Intersection         A        B      Combo      No. 2      No. 3    Recommended?

       Arsenal Street at West Site Drive      Yes     Yes       Yes       Yes        Yes           Yes



4
    Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices; Federal Highway Administration; Washington, DC; December 2009.
5
    Traffic Feasibility Study, Proposed Arbor Hill Residential Development, Weymouth, MA; prepared by Vanasse &
    Associates, Inc. September 1999.

Ron Müller & Associates                                              Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services              Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




As shown in this table, the proposed west site driveway intersection with Arsenal Street is
expected to meet all of the 8-hour volume warrants as well as the 4-hour and peak hour volume-
related signal warrants. Due to the anticipated traffic operations under STOP-sign control as
documented in Table 9, installation of a traffic control signal is therefore recommended.

In addition to signal control and to allow acceptable operations, it is recommended that Arsenal
Street be restriped and widened to provide an exclusive 11-foot wide left-turn lane and a single
11-foot wide through lane on the eastbound approach and a single 11-foot wide through lane and
an exclusive 10-foot wide right-turn lane on the westbound approach. An 8-foot wide on-street
parking lane should be maintained along the south side of Arsenal Street. On-street parking
along the north side of the street should be eliminated. An 8-foot wide 2-way bicycle path
should be constructed along the north side as further described below. The sidewalk along the
south side of the street should be maintained and a new sidewalk should be constructed along the
north side between the bike lane and the façade of the new building. The site driveway should
be constructed providing separate left- and right-turn lanes approaching Arsenal Street. The
recommended improvements are shown on the Conceptual Improvement Plan provided at the
end of this report. With implementation of these improvements, traffic operations can be greatly
improved as summarized in Table 11.


Arsenal Street at East Site Driveway and Beechwood Avenue

As shown in Table 9, the east site driveway would operate at LOS F with long delays for
vehicles exiting the driveway. These analyses do not consider the fact that the driveway is offset
from Beechwood Avenue by approximately 90 feet and that the queues resulting from the
Beechwood Avenue signal will block the site driveway most of the time during peak hours.
Actual operations are therefore expected to be worse than modeled. It is therefore recommended
that the east site driveway be incorporated into the Beechwood Avenue signal as the fourth leg to
the intersection. The driveway cannot be located directly opposite Beechwood Avenue as the
project proponent does not control the land. Therefore, the signal operation will have to provide
split-phasing between Beechwood Avenue and the driveway and longer clearance intervals will
have to be provided for Arsenal Street traffic. Although these measures tend to reduce the
efficiencies of the signal operation, they are necessary to provide safe operation and, as
documented in Table 11, will still provide acceptable traffic operations during peak hours.

In addition to incorporating the driveway into the signal operation, Arsenal Street should be
restriped and widened to provide an exclusive 10-foot wide left-turn lane and an 11-foot wide
through lane on the eastbound approach to ensure that through traffic is not impeded by any
vehicles waiting to turn left into the site. An 8-foot wide on-street parking lane should be
maintained along the south side of Arsenal Street. On the north side of Arsenal Street, an 8-foot
wide on-street parking lane should be provided for approximately 200 feet along with an 8-foot
wide 2-way bicycle path as further described below. The sidewalk along the south side of the
street should be maintained and a new sidewalk should be constructed along the north side
between the bike lane and the façade of the new building. Finally, the site driveway should be



13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                        Page 23
Ron Müller & Associates                                             Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services             Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




constructed to provide two approach lanes to Arsenal Street, including a shared left/through lane
and an exclusive right-turn lane. The recommended improvements are shown on the Conceptual
Improvement Plan provided at the end of this report.


Arsenal Street at Irving Street

Although acceptable traffic operations can be maintained under 2018 Build conditions without
any improvements, it is recommended that Arsenal Street be restriped to provide an exclusive
10-foot wide eastbound left-turn lane and an 11-foot wide westbound left-turn lane. The Irving
Street southbound approach should be restriped to provide an exclusive southbound left-turn lane
and a shared through/right-turn lane. This lane arrangement can be accomplished within the
existing pavement width of approximately 38 feet by providing two 11-foot wide approach lanes
(southbound) and one 16-foot wide receiving lane (northbound). New vehicle detection will be
required on the southbound Irving Street and Arsenal Street approaches to accommodate the new
geometry. With these improvements, the intersection can operate at desirable levels as
documents in Table 11. The recommended improvements are shown on the Conceptual
Improvement Plan provided at the end of this report.


Arsenal Street Between Irving Street and West Site Drive

East of Irving Street, Arsenal Street should be re-striped to provide an 8-foot wide on-street
parking lane on the south side, an 11-foot wide eastbound through lane, a raised 6-foot wide
median with shoulders, an 11-foot wide westbound through lane with a 3-foot shoulder, and an
8-foot wide 2-way bicycle path on the north side, as further described below. On-street parking
along the north side of the road should be eliminated. The recommended improvements are
shown on the Conceptual Improvement Plan provided at the end of this report.


Traffic Signal Coordination

The proposed west site driveway intersection with Arsenal Street will be located approximately
midway between the existing signals at Irving Street (650 feet) and at Beechwood Avenue (750
feet). Accordingly, it is recommended that the three signals be placed in a coordinated signal
system using time-based coordination. This will require updating the signal equipment at the
existing intersections to allow spread-spectrum radio coordination between the signals. Vehicle
detection will need to be provided on the Arsenal Street approaches as the existing intersections
are currently semi-actuated (i.e. detection only on the minor street approaches) and new signal
controllers will likely be required to accommodate the proposed changes. In addition, it is
recommended that a satellite GPS receiver be installed to automatically synchronize the internal
time clocks of the three signal controllers. This will ensure that time-of-day and day-of week
coordination programming will stay in sync.

          Bicycle and Pedestrian Accommodation

          In accordance with the Town of Watertown Bicycle Master Plan and the recommendations of the
          Bicycle and Pedestrian Committee, it is proposed that bicycle lanes be incorporated into the
          redesigned Arsenal Street in the site vicinity. Specifically, the existing bicycle lanes on Arsenal
          Street that currently end near the intersection with Louise Street should be extended westerly by
          providing an 8-foot wide 2-way bicycle path on the north side of the street to the intersection
          with Irving Street. Between Louise Street and Beechwood Avenue, this can be accomplished


          13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                                                   Page 27
Ron Müller & Associates                                                Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




within the existing street width by striping an 8-foot wide on-street parking lane on the south
side, a 13-foot wide eastbound travel lane, a 13-foot wide westbound travel lane, and an 8-foot
wide 2-way bicycle path separated from the parking lane by a 2-foot wide buffer. This buffer
can either be a raised divider with curbing on both sides, or flush with the pavement but
highlighted with stamped, colored concrete.

Between Beechwood Avenue and the west site driveway, the 2-way bicycle lane can be
incorporated into the design by widening Arsenal Street along the north side as described
previously. For approximately 200 feet to the west of the easterly site drive, on-street parking is
proposed and the bicycle path should again be separated from the parking lane by a 2-foot wide
buffer. This buffer can either be a raised divider with curbing on both sides, or flush with the
pavement but highlighted with stamped, colored concrete. West of the on-street parking lane on
the north side of the road, an exclusive right-turn lane is proposed for turns entering the west site
drive. The 2-way bicycle path should be separated from this right-turn lane by a 2-foot wide
buffer that is flush with the pavement so the buffer can also act as a shoulder for the right-turn
lane. The buffer in this area should be stamped, colored concrete.

Between the west site drive and Irving Street, Arsenal Street should be re-striped to provide an 8-
foot wide on-street parking lane on the south side, a 12-foot wide eastbound through lane, a 12-
foot wide westbound through lane, and an 8-foot wide 2-way bicycle path on the north side
separated from the travel lane by a 2-foot wide buffer. This buffer can either be a raised divider
with curbing on both sides, or flush with the pavement but highlighted with stamped, colored
concrete.

To enhance the safety of the proposed bicycle paths and raise driver awareness of the shared
road, particularly at intersections where vehicular and bicycle traffic have to cross, it is
recommended that "Bike Lane" and "Share the Road" signs be installed within the limits of work
as well as bicycle pavement markings and directional pavement arrows be striped in the bicycle
paths to clearly identify the lanes for bicycle use. At the existing signals at Irving Street and
Beechwood Avenue as well as the proposed signal at the west site driveway, it is recommended
that bicycle loop detectors be installed on the bike path approaches and that the signal timing be
adjusted to assure safe bicycle crossing through the intersections.

To promote safe pedestrian access to the site, it is recommended that a new sidewalk be
constructed along the north side of Arsenal Street between the proposed east and west site
driveways. Due to the locations of proposed buildings, this sidewalk will be of varying width,
but should be a minimum of 5 feet wide. The proposed supermarket and the 6,000 square foot
retail space will have pedestrian access directly from Arsenal Street. However, both site
driveways will also provide access to apartments and other retail space and pedestrian sidewalks
should therefore also be provided along these driveways to connect the Arsenal Street sidewalks
with these proposed uses. In addition, it is recommended that pedestrian crosswalks be striped
across both site driveways and across Arsenal Street at both driveway intersections and that an
exclusive pedestrian phase be incorporated into the new signal operation allowing safe pedestrian
access to and from the site. Wheelchair ramps and pedestrian push buttons should be installed at



13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                          Page 28
Ron Müller & Associates                                                  Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                  Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




all proposed crossings in conformance with Town of Watertown and Americans with Disabilities
Act (ADA) requirements. Finally, bicycle racks should be provided on site to allow safe storage
of bicycles and promote alternative modes of travel to the site. These proposed improvements
will further the goals of the Watertown Bicycle and Pedestrian Committee.

The design of the proposed 2-way bicycle path, sidewalks, wheelchair ramps and crosswalks is
shown on the Conceptual Improvement Plan provided at the end of this report.



CONCLUSIONS


Existing and future conditions at the study area intersections have been described and analyzed
with respect to traffic operations and the effect of the proposed site redevelopment. Conclusions
of this effort and recommendations are presented below.

·           The proposed project consists of razing the existing buildings to construct an
            approximately 40,000 square foot supermarket, 43,000 square feet of additional retail
            space, and 302 apartment units on the westerly portion of the development with access to
            Arsenal Street approximately midway between Irving Street and Beechwood Avenue.
            On the easterly portion of the development, approximately 6,000 square feet of retail
            space and 307 apartment units are proposed with access to Arsenal Street via the existing
            driveway slightly offset from the Beechwood Avenue. No site access is proposed onto
            any of the residential streets to the north of the site.

·           The combined redevelopment of the project site is expected to generate 420 new vehicle
            trips (147 in and 273 out) during the weekday AM peak hour, 714 new vehicle trips (408
            in and 306 out) during the weekday PM peak hour, and 791 new vehicle trips (413 in and
            378 out) during the Saturday midday peak hour.

·           Volume increases on Arsenal Street beyond the study area are expected in the range of
            114 to 210 vehicles during the peak hours. These increases represent, on average,
            approximately two to four additional vehicles per minute during the peak hours. On
            School Street, Mt. Auburn Street, Beechwood Avenue, and North Beacon Street, traffic
            volume increases between 47 and 129 vehicles are expected, or about one to two
            additional cars per minute, on average. Minimal increases in peak hour vehicle volumes
            are expected on Irving Street to the south of Arsenal Street (approximately one additional
            vehicle every two to 10 minutes) and on Palfrey Street (approximately one additional car
            every four to 30 minutes).

·           Redevelopment of the easterly (Webster) property will result in a reduction in volumes
            on the adjacent residential streets (Parker Street and Phillips Street) since access to a



13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                            Page 29
Ron Müller & Associates                                                    Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                    Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




            significant portion of the development on the Webster property will then be through the
            proposed site driveway on Arsenal Street.

·           Ample sight distances exist at the proposed site driveways onto Arsenal Street that
            exceed the minimum requirements. It is recommended that any proposed landscaping or
            signs in the vicinity of the driveways be kept low to the ground (less than 3 feet above
            street level) or set back sufficiently so as not to impede sight distances for drivers exiting
            the site.

·           Recommendations to improve traffic operations and intersection capacity as well as
            enhance pedestrian and bicycle travel through the corridor are proposed along Arsenal
            Street and are described below. A Conceptual Improvement Plan depicting the
            recommendations is provided at the end of this report.

·           To provide acceptable operations at the proposed west site driveway, it is recommended
            that a fully-actuated traffic control signal be installed and that Arsenal Street be widened
            and restriped to provide an exclusive left-turn lane and a single through lane in the
            eastbound direction and a single through lane and an exclusive right-turn lane in the
            westbound direction. The site driveway should be constructed providing separate left-
            and right-turn lanes.

·           To provide acceptable operations at the east site driveway, it is recommended that the
            driveway be incorporated into the Beechwood Avenue signal as the fourth leg to the
            intersection, albeit off-set from Beechwood Avenue. Arsenal Street should be widened
            and restriped to provide an exclusive left-turn lane and a single through lane in the
            eastbound direction.

·           Due to the proximity of the west site driveway to the Irving Street and Beechwood
            Avenue traffic signals, it is recommended that the three signals be placed in a coordinated
            signal system using time-based coordination. This will require updating of the existing
            signal equipment, including new signal controllers, loop detectors on Arsenal Street, and
            installation of a GPS receiver to synchronize the internal time clocks of the three signal
            controllers.

·           It is recommended that the Irving Street southbound approach to Arsenal Street be
            restriped to provide an exclusive southbound left-turn lane and a shared through/right-
            turn lane. Arsenal Street should be restriped to provide exclusive eastbound and
            westbound left-turn lanes. New vehicle detection will need to be installed at the
            intersection to accommodate the new lane arrangement.

·           On-street parking will be maintained along the south side of Arsenal Street, but be
            eliminated along the north side from Irving Street to just past the proposed west site
            drive.



13034 TIAS 121313.docx                                                                              Page 30
Ron Müller & Associates                                                   Traffic Impact and Access Study
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services                   Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts




·           A raised median is recommended along portions of Arsenal Street to provide streetscape
            elements with trees and landscaping. Access to existing curb cuts along Arsenal Street
            would be maintained through cuts in the median.

·           To further the goals of the Town of Watertown Bicycle Master Plan and the
            recommendations of the Bicycle and Pedestrian Committee, it is recommended that the
            bicycle lanes on Arsenal Street that currently end near the intersection with Louise Street
            be extended westerly to the intersection with Irving Street. A 2-way bicycle path can be
            created along the north side of Arsenal Street through a combination of roadway
            widening and restriping of that section of Arsenal Street; partial elimination of on-street
            parking; installation of "Bike Lane" and "Share the Road" signs; bicycle pavement
            markings; and installation of bicycle loop detectors at the affected signalized
            intersections.

·           To promote safe pedestrian access to the site, it is recommended that a new sidewalk be
            constructed on the north side of Arsenal Street between the east and west site driveways
            from the proposed 2-way bicycle path to the façade of the new buildings. I addition,
            sidewalks should be constructed along both site driveways and pedestrian crosswalks
            should be striped across both site driveways and across Arsenal Street at both driveway
            intersections. An exclusive pedestrian phase should be incorporated into the new traffic
            signal operation and wheelchair ramps and pedestrian push buttons should be installed at
            all proposed crossings to allow safe pedestrian access to and from the site and across
            Arsenal Street.

Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services         Mixed-Use Development, Watertown, Massachusetts

Capacity Analysis Methodology and Worksheets
Ron Müller & Associates                                             Capacity Analysis Methodology
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services




General

A primary result of capacity analysis is the assignment of levels of service to traffic facilities
under various traffic flow conditions. The capacity analysis methodology is based on the
concepts and procedures in the Highway Capacity Manual (HCM); Transportation Research
Board; Washington, D.C.; 2000. The concept of level of service (LOS) is defined as a
qualitative measure describing operational conditions within a traffic stream and their perception
by motorists and/or passengers. A level of service definition provides an index to quality of
traffic flow in terms of such factors as speed, travel time, freedom to maneuver, traffic
interruptions, comfort, convenience, and safety.

Six levels of service are defined for each type of facility. They are given letter designations from
A to F, with LOS A representing the best operating conditions and LOS F the worst. Since the
level of service of a traffic facility is a function of the traffic flows placed upon it, such a facility
may operate at a wide range of levels of service, depending on the time of day, day of week, or
period of year. A description of the operating condition under each level of service is provided
below:

     ·    LOS A describes conditions with little to no delay to motorists.

     ·    LOS B represents a desirable level with relatively low delay to motorists.

     ·    LOS C describes conditions with average delays to motorists.

     ·    LOS D describes operations where the influence of congestion becomes more noticeable.
          Delays are still within an acceptable range.

     ·    LOS E represents operating conditions with high delay values. This level is considered
          by many agencies to be the limit of acceptable delay.

     ·    LOS F is considered to be unacceptable to most drivers with high delay values that often
          occur, when arrival flow rates exceed the capacity of the intersection.



Unsignalized Intersections

Levels of service for unsignalized intersections are calculated using the operational analysis
methodology of the HCM. The procedure accounts for lane configuration on both the minor and
major street approaches, conflicting traffic stream volumes, and the type of intersection control
(STOP, YIELD, or all-way STOP control). The definition of level of service for unsignalized
intersections is a function of average control delay. Control delay includes initial deceleration
delay, queue move-up time, stopped delay, and final acceleration delay. The level-of-service
criteria for unsignalized intersections are shown in Table A-1.



                                                                                             Page 1 of 2
Ron Müller & Associates                                                   Capacity Analysis Methodology
Traffic Engineering and Consulting Services




Signalized Intersections

Levels of service for signalized intersections are also calculated using the operational analysis
methodology of the HCM. The methodology for signalized intersections assesses the effects of
signal type, timing, phasing, and progression; vehicle mix; and geometries on average control
delay. Control delay includes initial deceleration delay, queue move-up time, stopped delay, and
final acceleration delay. Table A-l summarizes the relationship between level of service and
average control delay.


                        Table A-1
                        Level-of-Service Criteria for Intersections


                                               Unsignalized Criteria     Signalized Criteria
                                              Average Control Delay    Average Control Delay
                           Level of Service   In Seconds Per Vehicle   In Seconds Per Vehicle

                                    A                  10                       10
                                    B              10.1 to 15.0             10.1 to 20.0
                                    C              15.1 to 25.0             20.1 to 35.0
                                    D              25.1 to 35.0             35.1 to 55.0
                                    E              35.1 to 50.0             55.1 to 80.0
                                    F                  >50                      >80




For signalized intersections, this delay criterion may be applied in assigning level of service
designations to individual lane groups, to individual intersection approaches, or to the entire
intersection. For unsignalized intersections, this delay criterion may be applied in assigning level
of service designations to individual lane groups or to individual intersection approaches.
